Results of HI estimation using MLP-256#

This notebook presents experimental results of anomaly detection on the Tennessee Eastman Process dataset using the model AutoEncoderMLP-256.

Importing libraries.

from ice.health_index_estimation.datasets import Milling
from ice.health_index_estimation.models import MLP

import pandas as pd
import numpy as np
import torch
from tqdm.auto import trange

Initializing model class and train/test data split

dataset_class = Milling()

data, target = dataset_class.df, dataset_class.target 
test_data, test_target = dataset_class.test, dataset_class.test_target

Training

metrics = []
for i in trange(5): # 5
    torch.random.manual_seed(i)
    model_class = MLP(
        window_size=64,
        stride=300,
        batch_size=258,
        lr=0.0004999805761074147,
        num_epochs=30,
        verbose=True,
        device='cuda'
    )
    model_class.fit(pd.concat(data), pd.concat(target))
    metrics.append(model_class.evaluate(pd.concat(test_data), pd.concat(test_target)))

mse_mean, mse_std = np.mean(mse, axis=0), np.std(mse, axis=0)

print(f'rmse: {np.mean(rmse):.8f} ± {2*np.std(rmse):.8f}')
print(f'mse: {np.mean(mse):.8f} ± {2*np.std(mse):.8f}')

rmse: 0.13118143 ± 0.01402841
mse: 0.01725777 ± 0.00376382
